$$f(A) = -0.10017\sqrt{A} + 0.47149\sin(0.8555A)$$

Note that the GT depends only on A (not t), so any candidate that has t-dependent terms must be able to zero them out.

Let me systematically check candidates that could produce $\sqrt{A}$ and $\sin(A)$ terms.

**Key observations about GT:**
- Contains $\sqrt{A} = A^{0.5}$, which requires either $A^{c}$ with $c=0.5$ or similar
- Contains $\sin(cA)$, a sinusoidal function of A
- No dependence on t

**Candidate 18:** $c_0 e^{c_1 t} + c_2 e^{c_3 t} + c_4 e^{c_5 t}\sin(Ac_6 + c_7)$

Set $c_1=0, c_3=0, c_5=0$: becomes $c_0 + c_2 + c_4\sin(Ac_6 + c_7)$. This gives a constant plus $\sin(cA + \phi)$, but can't produce $\sqrt{A}$. No match.

**Candidate 41:** $A^{c_0}c_1 + c_2 t/(c_3+c_4 e^{c_5 t}) + c_6\exp(c_7\sin(Ac_8+c_9))$

Set $c_2=0$ to kill t-dependence. Becomes $c_1 A^{c_0} + c_6\exp(c_7\sin(c_8 A + c_9))$. The exponential of sine can't simplify to $\sin$ plus $A^{0.5}$. No match.

**Candidate 30:** $c_0 A e^{c_1 A} + c_2 e^{c_3 t} + c_4 e^{c_5 t}\sin(c_6 A + c_7)$

Set $c_3=0, c_5=0$: becomes $c_0 A e^{c_1 A} + c_2 + c_4\sin(c_6 A + c_7)$. Need $c_0 A e^{c_1 A}$ to equal $-0.10017\sqrt{A} + \text{const}$. Can't match $\sqrt{A}$ with $Ae^{cA}$. No match.

**Candidate 6:** $c_0 A e^{c_1 A} + c_2 A/(A+c_3) + c_4 e^{c_5 t} + c_6(A+c_7)^{c_8}$

Set $c_4=0$ (kill t). Becomes $c_0 A e^{c_1 A} + c_2 A/(A+c_3) + c_6(A+c_7)^{c_8}$. This has $(A+c_7)^{c_8}$ which with $c_7=0, c_8=0.5$ gives $c_6\sqrt{A}$. But no $\sin$ term. No match.

**Candidate 16:** $A^2 c_0 + Ac_1/(A+c_2) + c_3 t/(c_4+t^2) + c_5\sin(c_6\log(A^2 c_7+1)+c_8)$

Set $c_3=0$ to kill t, $c_0=0$. Becomes $c_1 A/(A+c_2) + c_5\sin(c_6\log(c_7 A^2+1)+c_8)$.

Can $c_6\log(c_7 A^2+1)$ approximate $c \cdot A$? No, $\log$ and linear are fundamentally different. No exact match.

**Candidate 39:** $A^2 c_0 + A^2 c_1 + Ac_2 + c_3\sin(c_4\log(A^2 c_5+1)+c_6) + c_7/A^5$

Same issue - $\sin(\log(\cdot))$ can't become $\sin(cA)$.

After checking all candidates, none can simultaneously produce both $\sqrt{A}$ (requiring $A^{0.5}$) and $\sin(cA)$ terms. The candidates with $A^{c}$ terms don't have $\sin(cA)$, and those with $\sin$ terms don't have $A^{c}$ with fractional exponents (or have $\sin$ of $\log$ rather than $\sin$ of $A$).
